<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_6950784">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/6950784" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/431061-jeff" class="left imgcol" title="Jeff"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1233435769p2/431061.jpg" alt="Jeff" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/6950784?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 28, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/431061-jeff" class="user" title="Jeff">Jeff</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6690.Danny_the_Champion_of_the_World" title="Hardcover 9780375814259" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer6950784">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2253154015071268507">Oddly to some, this still stands as my favorite Roald Dahl book. It's hard for me to pinpoint why, since it's my opinion and I hate examining my opinions too closely, but to take a swing at it:<br />It's one of the least zany of Dahl's books, which ultimately gives it staying power. With many of his other works, you get caught up in the wacky characters, situations, and goings ons and it's hard to take them as seriously once you get a little bit older and gain a little bit of sophistication. However,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2253154015071268507">Oddly to some, this still stands as my favorite Roald Dahl book. It's hard for me to pinpoint why, since it's my opinion and I hate examining my opinions too closely, but to take a swing at it:<br />It's one of the least zany of Dahl's books, which ultimately gives it staying power. With many of his other works, you get caught up in the wacky characters, situations, and goings ons and it's hard to take them as seriously once you get a little bit older and gain a little bit of sophistication. However, DTCOTW (wow, won't be writing that again) contains some of Dahl's best pure writing as the author beautifully and at times almost lyrically describes the relationship between Danny and his father. <br />I think this book very often gets overlooked and I think that's a shame, because it's so very good. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2253154015071268507">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1459592433">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1459592433" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5448792-brendon-schrodinger" class="left imgcol" title="Brendon Schrodinger"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1392261804p2/5448792.jpg" alt="Brendon Schrodinger" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1459592433?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 03, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5448792-brendon-schrodinger" class="user" title="Brendon Schrodinger">Brendon Schrodinger</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1121503.Danny_the_Champion_of_the_World" title="Paperback 9780141322674" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5448792-brendon-schrodinger?shelf=childrens" class="actionLinkLite">childrens</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1459592433">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17906056855801473148">"Danny the Champion of the World", like most of Roald's work, can be seen in two different ways. Danny, 10 years old, lives with his father in gypsy caravan behind a filling station in rural England. His father is a mechanic and teaches Danny very early how to rebuild engines and be a brilliant mechanic. But his father has another hobby that was secret to Danny. When Danny finds out about it, his father brings him along. Family bonding, much happiness. Very sweet book.<br /><br />Or it could be the tale of</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17906056855801473148">"Danny the Champion of the World", like most of Roald's work, can be seen in two different ways. Danny, 10 years old, lives with his father in gypsy caravan behind a filling station in rural England. His father is a mechanic and teaches Danny very early how to rebuild engines and be a brilliant mechanic. But his father has another hobby that was secret to Danny. When Danny finds out about it, his father brings him along. Family bonding, much happiness. Very sweet book.<br /><br />Or it could be the tale of a petty thief who recruits his 10 year old son into the fold and introduces him into a conspiracy of thieves that includes the local doctor and even the constabulary. <br /><br />But in the end it comes down to the lesson of 'you can do anything you like to people who are assholes', which is pretty much a common theme in all Dahl's books.<br /><br />Reading it as an adult is no less magical as reading it as a ten years old. This time I found myself in his father's shoes as opposed to Danny's. And while I may not have made the same decisions about my son as William, I can see why he did it and I can feel his immense love for Danny.<br /><br />I's funny how the same images in your mind crop up over 20 years from reading a book. But the descriptions painted the same pictures as they did all those years ago. One thing that I did notice though, is that this time the illustrations were by Quintin Blake, who we all adore. But the copy that I read and reread from my local library had a different illustrator. I'll try and find a copy of this on eBay as it probably matches the images in my mind much more.<br /><br />So, recommended highly. Read it as a parent and a grown up. And remember to be SPARKY!<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449205051i/17251263._SY540_.jpg" /><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17906056855801473148">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1352332597">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1352332597" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3533262-stacey-prettybooks" class="left imgcol" title="Stacey (prettybooks)"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1429995380p2/3533262.jpg" alt="Stacey (prettybooks)" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1352332597?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 09, 2016</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3533262-stacey-prettybooks" class="user" title="Stacey (prettybooks)">Stacey (prettybooks)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7137672-danny-the-champion-of-the-world" title="Paperback 9780141326177" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=classics" class="actionLinkLite">classics</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=read-in-my-twenties" class="actionLinkLite">read-in-my-twenties</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=childrens-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">childrens-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=classics-challenge" class="actionLinkLite">classics-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1352332597">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3391377255681575756"><em>This post is part of the <a rel="nofollow" href="https://theprettybooks.wordpress.com/2014/12/27/2015-classics-challenge/" title="2015 Classics Challenge">2015 Classics Challenge</a>.</em><br /><br /><em>"A stodgy parent is no fun at all. What a child wants and deserves is a parent who is SPARKY".</em><br /><br />Danny thinks his dad is the most marvellous and exciting father a boy could wish for. Life is happy and peaceful in their gipsy caravan, until one day Danny discovers his dad has been breaking the law. What's more, soon Danny has to join his father as they attempt to pull off a daring and devilish plot against their horrible, greedy neighbour, Mr Victor H</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3391377255681575756"><em>This post is part of the <a rel="nofollow" href="https://theprettybooks.wordpress.com/2014/12/27/2015-classics-challenge/" title="2015 Classics Challenge">2015 Classics Challenge</a>.</em><br /><br /><em>"A stodgy parent is no fun at all. What a child wants and deserves is a parent who is SPARKY".</em><br /><br />Danny thinks his dad is the most marvellous and exciting father a boy could wish for. Life is happy and peaceful in their gipsy caravan, until one day Danny discovers his dad has been breaking the law. What's more, soon Danny has to join his father as they attempt to pull off a daring and devilish plot against their horrible, greedy neighbour, Mr Victor Hazell.<br /><br /><strong>WHEN I Discovered This Classic</strong><br />It came in my lovely Roald Dahl box set, full of 15 wonderful Dahl novels. I didn't know anything about it at all, except that it was my friend Caitlin's favourite Dahl story.<br /><br /><strong>WHY I Chose to Read It </strong><br />I've enjoyed reading Roald Dahl novels over the past couple of years. I haven't read one this year, so I thought it was about time. I chose <em>Danny the Champion of the World</em> because it's one that a lot of people seem to adore and yet is completely new to me, compared to some of the previous stories I've read, like <a rel="nofollow" href="https://theprettybooks.wordpress.com/2014/12/16/thoughts-on-roald-dahl-the-bfg-the-witches-fantastic-mr-fox/">
  <em>The Witches</em>
</a> and <a rel="nofollow" href="https://theprettybooks.wordpress.com/2013/10/21/thoughts-on-roald-dahl-matilda-esio-trot-the-twits/">
  <em>Matilda</em>
</a>. I also haven't read any classics with illustrations this year, so I was looking forward to spending time with Quentin Blake's brilliant pictures.<br /><br /><strong>WHAT Makes It A Classic<br /></strong>Roald Dahl's stories are like being inside a child's brain. They're full of humour and adventure. They're full of incompetent adults and loving adults. They're full of wonderful things to remember, like the quote at the top of this review. As I discovered when I first read <em>Matilda</em>, Roald Dahl's stories can also be enjoyed immensely by adults.<br /><br /><em>"Most of the really exciting things we do in our lives scare us to death. They wouldn't be exciting if they didn't".</em><br /><br /><strong>WHAT I Thought of This Classic<br /></strong>It's different to Roald Dahl's other stories in that it feels more contemporary compared to the fun and whimsical stories I've come across so far. I adored that Danny's father would tell him stories, referencing Roald Dahl's other work, like <em>The BFG</em> and <em>Witches</em>. As I've read both of these, I enjoyed it very much. I remember there being a lot of chat about fictional fathers this year on Father's Day, and Danny's popped up as being one of the best dads in fiction. I can see why – he's a brilliant father. He's protective and yet will send Danny on exciting adventures. He tells wonderful stories and is incredibly intelligent. Danny's a happy child. His life isn't full of expensive things or luxury, but it's full of interesting and fulfilling experiences, and a lot of love, all down to his dad. Although <em>Danny the Champion of the World</em> isn't one of my Dahl favourites, it was a joy to read. I was ready for awful Mr Hazell to get his comeuppance!<br /><br /><strong>WILL It Stay A Classic<br /></strong>I think it'll be a terrible year, the year that Roald Dahl's novels stop being read. I cannot imagine that this will ever happen.<br /><br /><strong>WHO I’d Recommend It To<br /></strong>People who love children's stories, funny stories and heartwarming stories. People who haven't yet read a Roald Dahl novel and are a little wary about delving into the more eccentric stories. People who are young at heart.<br /><br /><em>I also reviewed this book over on <a rel="nofollow" href="http://theprettybooks.wordpress.com/book-reviews/">Pretty Books</a>.</em></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3391377255681575756">...more</a>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown">
    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_6902801">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/6902801" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/395599-shannon-giraffe-days" class="left imgcol" title="Shannon (Giraffe Days)"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1420332941p2/395599.jpg" alt="Shannon (Giraffe Days)" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/6902801?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 11, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/395599-shannon-giraffe-days" class="user" title="Shannon (Giraffe Days)">Shannon (Giraffe Days)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/531756.Danny_the_Champion_of_the_World" title="Paperback 9780140309126" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/395599-shannon-giraffe-days?shelf=childrens" class="actionLinkLite">childrens</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/395599-shannon-giraffe-days?shelf=re-read" class="actionLinkLite">re-read</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/395599-shannon-giraffe-days?shelf=2010" class="actionLinkLite">2010</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/395599-shannon-giraffe-days?shelf=my-childhood" class="actionLinkLite">my-childhood</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer6902801">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9834283825477106051">I got this book in 1988, when I was eight or nine years old, and it was a dear favourite of mine. The story of Danny and his fantastic dad, and their life in the old gypsy caravan by the petrol pumps and garage - it was at once a whole new other world, and something very near and dear to me.<br /><br />Danny is raised by his dad, a mechanic and Danny's hero. They live in a colourful wooden caravan under a large apple tree, serving petrol and fixing cars. Danny's father teaches him all about cars and how to</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9834283825477106051">I got this book in 1988, when I was eight or nine years old, and it was a dear favourite of mine. The story of Danny and his fantastic dad, and their life in the old gypsy caravan by the petrol pumps and garage - it was at once a whole new other world, and something very near and dear to me.<br /><br />Danny is raised by his dad, a mechanic and Danny's hero. They live in a colourful wooden caravan under a large apple tree, serving petrol and fixing cars. Danny's father teaches him all about cars and how to fix them, and Danny is a great help in the garage. At night his dad tells him fabulous stories, and when Danny starts school at seven, his dad walks him there and back every day. Danny has the best life, and he loves his dad more than anything.<br /><br />Then one night Danny wakes up to find his dad missing. Anxious, because it is the first time his father has disappeared like this, Danny waits up for him. When his father returns, Danny learns that his dad has a secret: he's a pheasant poacher! His own dad was one before him and came up with several ingenius ways of poaching the birds, and Danny's own mother used to join him on poaching nights. This night marked the first night Danny's father had been out in the private woods - owned by the brutish Mr Victor Hazell - since Danny was born.<br /><br />And so, Danny's father introduces Danny into the world of pheasant poaching - and Danny discovers that virtually the entire town enjoys a spot of pheasant poaching! Even the doctor and the policeman and the minister's wife is involved - and no one likes Mr Hazell, with his "tiny piggy eyes" and "smug superior little smile". But it is Danny himself who comes up with the most clever poaching plan ever conceived - a way to steal all one hundred and twenty birds at once, the night before Mr Hazell's shooting party arrives!<br /><br />Perhaps because of the different illustrator, or perhaps because it is more of a realistic and human story than many of Dahl's other, <em>Danny the Champion of the World</em> has a different tone and feel to it than classics like <em>The Witches</em> and <em>The BFG</em>. It is more like his memoir of his childhood, <em>Boy</em>, and similar works. It is written for children, and has humour and a lightness of spirit to it, but it is also more serious. In keeping the story "real", though, Dahl shows just how fantastic our real lives can be, without giants and witches and other fantastical things.<br /><br />It is also a story of one boy's childhood in what I figure was the early 50s, and as such it reads like a story of a completely by-gone era. The chances of someone now having a childhood like Danny's is pretty slim, and so there's something nostalgic about his story - perhaps, again, inspired by Dahl's own childhood, not in the details of the story but in the characters, and the mischief. It's also nostalgic in that small English village way, where everyone knows everyone's secrets, finds clever ways of pulling the wool over the eyes of people they don't like, and can generally be counted upon in a pinch.<br /><br />In the schemes for poaching pheasants, there is definitely a touch of the wildly flamboyant Dahl we all know and love: "The Horse-hair Stopper" and "The Sticky Hat"; and in the description of oafish and cruel Victor Hazell. Danny's father, who's never named, is a fantastic figure, and when Danny calls him the best father in the world, you find yourself easily agreeing with him. Well, he may be at times irresponsible and a little wild, but he has the qualities you want in a great father - and this is Dahl's message, proudly spelled out at the back of the book:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  A MESSAGE<br />to Children Who Have Read This Book<br /><br />When you grow up<br />and have children of your own<br />do please remember something important<br /><br />a stodgy parent is <em>no fun at all</em><br /><br />What a child wants<br /><em>and deserves</em><br />is a parent who is <br /><br />SPARKY
</blockquote><br /><br />It's great, even as an adult, to come to that at the end of the book (something I had completely forgotten was there) and be reminded of what I loved and admired in adults when I was a kid. I loved the artist friend of my parents who, when he and his wife came over for dinner, would take the time to entertain us with magic tricks and make us laugh. Or my nanna when she would put me on her lap and read fairy tales to me. Or my dad (and grandad) when he'd lie on his back in the passage, put me on his feet, and toss me over his head, always catching me and setting me on my feet. Learning about plants with my mum. These are the memories we keep, after all - the ones that chase the darker shadows away. It seems like the current trend in parenting is to fill your kids' days with activities, sport, hobbies, studies, rather than spend time having fun with them. Or even to buy horrid plastic toy sets and computer games for toddlers and older - it's so much better to let kids invent their own games, make their own toys and things out of random household odds and ends and scraps, and play amongst themselves. <br /><br />Danny's inventiveness in the poaching scheme earns well-deserved praise from his dad and others, and his father calls him the champion of the world - far from being a form of gross steroid to a child's self-esteem, it humbles Danny but leaves him re-affirmed in the greatness of his one remaining parent. The two are a close family unit who share everything with each other, and so it doesn't matter that they're poor, that they live in a little caravan with just a little paraffin stove to heat up food on: they have each other, and love, and great stories and fantastic adventures. Having money isn't the key to happiness, is I think Dahl's other message here.<br /><br />On a side note, it was interesting reading this after so many years, because I had a vivid memory of one of Bennett's illustrations at the very end of the book, <em>which doesn't exist</em>! I remembered it ending - with accompanying illustration - with all the pheasants roosting in the apple tree above the caravan. I must have invented this ending for myself, as a child, and improved upon it each time I read it until it supplanted the real ending in my head. I've done this with other things from my childhood, so it wouldn't surprise me in the least. It is the ending I would have liked, but not a realistic one!<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9834283825477106051">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1405106030">

  <a href="/user/show/71601-philip" class="left imgcol" title="Philip"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1319511845p2/71601.jpg" alt="Philip" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1405106030?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 30, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/71601-philip" class="user" title="Philip">Philip</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/763167.Danny_the_Champion_of_the_World" title="Paperback 9780141301143" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/71601-philip?shelf=classics" class="actionLinkLite">classics</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/71601-philip?shelf=young-adult" class="actionLinkLite">young-adult</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/71601-philip?shelf=children" class="actionLinkLite">children</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/71601-philip?shelf=eleanor-review" class="actionLinkLite">eleanor-review</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/71601-philip?shelf=gwennie-review" class="actionLinkLite">gwennie-review</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/71601-philip?shelf=poppy-review" class="actionLinkLite">poppy-review</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1405106030">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14493798652705986033">For the record, this was not <em>my</em> favorite Roald Dahl book. Something about the poaching seemed a little less "Robin Hood" and a little more... Uh... "sour grapes" than what I was hoping for. But whatever. It was still good.<br /><br />And, it was one of the very, very few Roald Dahl books I'd never read. Either way, lets see what the kids said about it. (If it gets 4 or 5 stars, you know why...)<br /><br />Dad: Alright! How many stars do you want to give it?<br /><br />Eleanor: FIVE! <br /><br />Gwennie: FIIIiiiiiVVEE? <br /><br />E: Gwennie, you don't so</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14493798652705986033">For the record, this was not <em>my</em> favorite Roald Dahl book. Something about the poaching seemed a little less "Robin Hood" and a little more... Uh... "sour grapes" than what I was hoping for. But whatever. It was still good.<br /><br />And, it was one of the very, very few Roald Dahl books I'd never read. Either way, lets see what the kids said about it. (If it gets 4 or 5 stars, you know why...)<br /><br />Dad: Alright! How many stars do you want to give it?<br /><br />Eleanor: FIVE! <br /><br />Gwennie: FIIIiiiiiVVEE? <br /><br />E: Gwennie, you don't sound so sure.<br /><br />G: Five? Maybe five?<br /><br />(These reviews are getting harder to do, now that Gwennie can read. She's reading everything I type.)<br /><br />D: We are giving it 5 stars, right?<br /><br />G&amp;E: Right.<br /><br />D: What did you think about the book?<br /><br />E: Wait. Who are you starting with? Can we go in birthday order? So, Gwen goes first, because it's her birthday next.<br /><br />G: Birthday? Wait. Why did you write birthday?<br /><br />E: Because of birthday order. November is after October. And November is your birthday month, so you get to go next. *Lists off months with a whistling/wind noise between each one.*<br /><br />D: So Gwen goes first.<br /><br />E: Because it's her birthday next.<br /><br />Poppy: (From outside the room): And then I go second, and then Eleanor goes last. *Poppy has not read the book with us. Also, her birthday is after Eleanor's. Here's hoping there's not a fight brewing over this... Back to Gwen*<br /><br />G: Good. I liked it.<br /><br />D: What did you like about the book?<br /><br />G: The cane? The cane part?<br /><br />E: The cane part? What does that have to do with Danny Champion of the World? Where there was a cane laying in the middle of the sidewalk.<br /><br />G: *Shyly shaking her head and tapping her hand* ... ... .... .... Nooooo... The school cane.<br /><br />E: OOOOOOoooooo!!!! I know what you're talking about! Where Danny gets hit on the hand with the cane!<br /><br />*Gwen nods*<br /><br />D: Gwennie, so you liked the part with the cane in the school?<br /><br />*Gwennie nods*<br /><br />D: What did you like about it, Gwen?<br /><br />G: I'm not sure why I liked it.<br /><br />D: So, you liked the fact that he got hit?<br /><br />G: No.<br /><br />D: You liked it because you remember it?<br /><br />G: Yeah.<br /><br />D: Because it was interesting and you're glad it doesn't happen anymore?<br /><br />G: Yeah.<br /><br />D: El, what was your favorite part?<br /><br />Eleanor: <em>I</em> liked the pheasant part. And the pheasants on the car. Where <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[Mr. Hazell was like, "GET THOSE PHEASANTS OFF MY CAR!!!! GET THOSE DISGUSTING BIRDS OFF MY CAR!!!!" <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />D: Girls, who was your favorite character in the book?<br /><br />G: Uhhh. The dad.<br /><br />E: I liked the dad and Danny. AND everybody else. I had a dream about Danny Champion of the World. Well, it was similar to that. It was about Danny, but it wasn't exactly the same. They were at the store, and Mr. Hazell came in, and Danny's dad gave Danny one of those "funny looks" and suddenly they were both outside. And then, they poured protein - like hard boiled protein that's been in eggs already - they poured lots and lots of it on Mr. Victor Hazell, and they.... and it got all over the ground, and there was a whole bunch. And it got all over their leg. Like, right up to HERE on their leg. (Shows me on her leg.) It would be lower on your leg, because you're taller. And then they fell, and they rolled all over the place, but it didn't hurt because there was so much egg white and protein all over the place. Mr. Victor Hazell and the pheasants drove away really fast, and they poured more egg white all over the place, and-<br /><br />D: Wait, who poured egg white all over the place? Mr. Victor Hazell?<br /><br />E: Well, I guess it was tracked out into the streets, because it was all over his car, too. And then there was more falling over, and rolling around. And then, they had ice cream. The cause of the celebration was that they'd never have to see Mr. Victor Hazell again. And, in the dream, it was a bright sunny day, but the egg whites made it look like snow.<br /><br />D: I'm not sure that this is actually a review of the book, but I love it when you (or I) get into a book so much that we start dreaming about it.<br /><br />E: Well, that's the dream.<br /><br />D: Gwennie, anything else to add? Anything else you want me to say about the book that you really like? Gwennie, was there anything you didn't like in the book?<br /><br />G: Well, nothing made me sad or scared. So, no. ...Well, actually, I didn't like when they stole Mr. Victor Hazell's pheasants, and when the dad left Danny alone. I thought he shouldn't do that. He shouldn't leave his kids without telling them.<br /><br />D: Did you get worried that we would leave you without telling you?<br /><br />G: No. (Shakes head very sincerely.) (Very sweetly again says) No.<br /><br />D: Gwen, of course we'd never leave you without telling you.<br /><br />G: *Smiles* I know.<br /><br />D: Is that it?<br /><br />E: Poppy? Anything you want to say about the book?<br /><br />P: Yeah. GOOD!<br /><br />E: Poppy says it was a good book.<br /><br />(Again, for the record, Poppy didn't read it with us.)<!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>

      <a href="/user/show/10982678-claire-stevens" class="user" title="Claire Stevens">Claire Stevens</a>

        rated it

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a href="/review/list/10982678-claire-stevens?shelf=kids" class="actionLinkLite">kids</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1306941837">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10641707821770669558">This is one of my favourite Roald Dahl books. It's simply the story of a boy, Danny, and his father, who is a pheasant poacher. That's it. It's one of his least crazy books and doesn't involve magic at all. Admittedly there is a huge madcap caper at the end, but it never truly pushes the boundaries of believability.<br /><br />The story deals with all sorts of problems that children have growing up, including school and bullying and it's as relevant now as it was when it was written (apart form the use of c</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10641707821770669558">This is one of my favourite Roald Dahl books. It's simply the story of a boy, Danny, and his father, who is a pheasant poacher. That's it. It's one of his least crazy books and doesn't involve magic at all. Admittedly there is a huge madcap caper at the end, but it never truly pushes the boundaries of believability.<br /><br />The story deals with all sorts of problems that children have growing up, including school and bullying and it's as relevant now as it was when it was written (apart form the use of corporal punishment in schools, thank god). It's also incredibly cosy reading. Danny and his dad live in an old gypsy caravan underneath an apple tree out the back of their garage. They have a gaslamp for lighting and a small stove and bunk beds. See? So cosy.<br /><br />This book also taught me several methods for poaching pheasants and trout. Which obviously I would never do.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1278237-elisha-condie?shelf=childrens" class="actionLinkLite">childrens</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer171137232">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3062112190824251412"> This is one of the sweetest books in the entire world. Danny and his father live in a little gypsy caravan behind the filling station where they work. Danny's Mum died ages ago and it's just the two of them and they are very happy together. <br /><br /> Then one day his Dad tells him about poaching, and how exciting it is. He teaches Danny the best ways to steal birds off the mean rich man's land and they hatch a plan to steal ALL of them the night before the big hunt to humiliate the mean rich man. But th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3062112190824251412"> This is one of the sweetest books in the entire world. Danny and his father live in a little gypsy caravan behind the filling station where they work. Danny's Mum died ages ago and it's just the two of them and they are very happy together. <br /><br /> Then one day his Dad tells him about poaching, and how exciting it is. He teaches Danny the best ways to steal birds off the mean rich man's land and they hatch a plan to steal ALL of them the night before the big hunt to humiliate the mean rich man. But things don't run smoothly and they end up having to improvise (with the help of half the town, also in on the poaching game). <br /><br /> I loved reading this with my little girl. Danny and his Dad are best friends and have the best conversations and interactions. It was funny and sweet and we both loved it. It's been my favorite Dahl book we've read together. I kept thinking about how Roald's father died when he was very small and how he never knew him at all, and I wondered if this father and Danny were exactly what Dahl wished he had. <br /><br /> This was a lovely little book. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3062112190824251412">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5610126164907094727">Another lovely book by Roald Dahl. Danny and his father live in a small gypsy caravan, and work together fixing cars and manning a gas pump. The bond between Danny and his dad is absolutely fabulous, and I think as a kid, I would have loved living in that caravan. Danny's dad has a terrible secret - he loves to poach pheasants. The story was incredibly sweet. The only thing that made me uncomfortable was the fact that they're essentially killing animals to eat them. Now, I'm not a vegetarian or</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5610126164907094727">Another lovely book by Roald Dahl. Danny and his father live in a small gypsy caravan, and work together fixing cars and manning a gas pump. The bond between Danny and his dad is absolutely fabulous, and I think as a kid, I would have loved living in that caravan. Danny's dad has a terrible secret - he loves to poach pheasants. The story was incredibly sweet. The only thing that made me uncomfortable was the fact that they're essentially killing animals to eat them. Now, I'm not a vegetarian or animal activist, but something like that does make me feel slightly iffy. It was still a lovely story though</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer886711199">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer219907027902996632">Book review 11 – Danny the Champion of the World – Roald Dahl<br /><br />This is one of my favourite Roald Dahl books. It was bought for me as a present and since then, has always remained in my heart. This is a magnificent story of strong, and angelic relationship between a boy and his father and how their bond takes them on an unforgettable journey. Danny lives with his Dad in a simple caravan behind their petrol station. They live a happy life and both Danny and his dad enjoy each other’s company immense</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText219907027902996632">Book review 11 – Danny the Champion of the World – Roald Dahl<br /><br />This is one of my favourite Roald Dahl books. It was bought for me as a present and since then, has always remained in my heart. This is a magnificent story of strong, and angelic relationship between a boy and his father and how their bond takes them on an unforgettable journey. Danny lives with his Dad in a simple caravan behind their petrol station. They live a happy life and both Danny and his dad enjoy each other’s company immensely. However, one night Danny wakes up in the middle of the night to find out his dad is not in his bed. It turns out that his father is hiding a secret. This secret leads Danny to be the Champion of the World. Superbly written by Roal Dahl, this book is much loved through out the world and both, child and parent can connect with this book on many different levels. I also believe that this book provides an ointment for parents in the modern era to spend precious time with their children. This book can be enjoyed by both young and old and I hope that one day I can read this book to my future class. <br /></span>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/69535362?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 31, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2246621-dana-salman" class="user" title="Dana Salman">Dana Salman</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6690.Danny_the_Champion_of_the_World" title="Hardcover 9780375814259" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2246621-dana-salman?shelf=boring-books" class="actionLinkLite">boring-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer69535362">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7495731924006207723">A bit far-fetched. I'd passed by this book many times before and it never caught my interest on account of it being long and the title not being more discriptive. You could be the champion of the world through many things; doing something exceedingly difficult or impossible, inventing something that could cure world hunger, or something else equally huge. Drugging two hundred pheasants is not exactly what I had in mind. All that crap Danny's father talks about poaching being an art. Who in their</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7495731924006207723">A bit far-fetched. I'd passed by this book many times before and it never caught my interest on account of it being long and the title not being more discriptive. You could be the champion of the world through many things; doing something exceedingly difficult or impossible, inventing something that could cure world hunger, or something else equally huge. Drugging two hundred pheasants is not exactly what I had in mind. All that crap Danny's father talks about poaching being an art. Who in their right minds would consider stealing an art? I mean, if it were for the greater good I can see about doing it at all, but because you YEARN to do it? What's so fun about trying to steal a couple of stupid birds when the consequences include going to jail or getting shot? If you ask me, this might've been a bit more interesting if Danny HAD landed in jail. But he didn't, and it's not. It was boring. Long and boring, the worst of combinations. I didn't exactly hate it, but it's not something I would go out of my way to re-read. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7495731924006207723">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6690.Danny_the_Champion_of_the_World" title="Hardcover 9780375814259" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer318621451">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2764187580670904515"> The book follows a young primary school child who tells his story of his life and his father's. The story mainly centres around the child's love for his father and how best to trap pheasants, while evading the aristocrat character who owns the woods where the birds live.<br /> I was fairly disappointed by this book from a renowned author as there was a very weak storyline that did not engage me. At times it felt as though the author was trying to just fill the pages with laborious and pointless diver</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2764187580670904515"> The book follows a young primary school child who tells his story of his life and his father's. The story mainly centres around the child's love for his father and how best to trap pheasants, while evading the aristocrat character who owns the woods where the birds live.<br /> I was fairly disappointed by this book from a renowned author as there was a very weak storyline that did not engage me. At times it felt as though the author was trying to just fill the pages with laborious and pointless diversions away from the main story, that again failed to spark my interest. The writing is best suited to KS2 and perhaps early secondary school with illustrations typical of their style. The children who would read this book will need a much better attention span as well as imagination than I have, as I had found it rather difficult to find anything good about the book. Perhaps those with an interest in poultry will find this story more to their liking than I did. Fantastic author but not because of this book.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2764187580670904515">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <a href="/user/show/116652-punk" class="left imgcol" title="Punk"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1181025939p2/116652.jpg" alt="Punk" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/5440914?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 31, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/116652-punk" class="user" title="Punk">Punk</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/24953.Danny_The_Champion_Of_The_World" title="Hardcover 9780224064699" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/116652-punk?shelf=young-adult" class="actionLinkLite">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer5440914">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6874893918314568147">YA. I got this book as a reward for participating in my library's summer reading program back when I was still short enough to read for cash and prizes. Ironically enough, I never read it. Sab instructed me to do so, and I finally dug it out and gave it a go. <br /><br />This is a book about Danny and the very best father a boy could ever want. There's something a tad creepy about a boy who idolizes his father this much, but I'm not a boy living alone with his father in the English countryside in the 1970s,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6874893918314568147">YA. I got this book as a reward for participating in my library's summer reading program back when I was still short enough to read for cash and prizes. Ironically enough, I never read it. Sab instructed me to do so, and I finally dug it out and gave it a go. <br /><br />This is a book about Danny and the very best father a boy could ever want. There's something a tad creepy about a boy who idolizes his father this much, but I'm not a boy living alone with his father in the English countryside in the 1970s, so who's to say. The other thing that made me uncomfortable was how lovingly these characters took to poaching pheasants. Just because someone's rich and mean doesn't make it okay to steal their birds for fun. Dahl is well known for his whimsy and magic, and the way he writes about the ways to trap pheasants is silly and clever, but my stupid morals got in the way. If he'd made up an animal for Danny and his father (and really, the whole town) to poach, it would have been much easier for me to take.<br /><br />This is probably my least favorite Dahl. It's also one of the few I didn't read as a child, so maybe there's a connection, but I just didn't like it.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6874893918314568147">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5623625005079423375">In either year 2 or 3 (actually I think it happened both years) my class had a substitute teacher at the end of the year.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText5623625005079423375">In either year 2 or 3 (actually I think it happened both years) my class had a substitute teacher at the end of the year. She was amazing and I adored her. She would always read us stories which of course I loved. As well as this book she also read us Roald Dahls The Witches and The BFG.<br /><br />Anyways I was totally enthralled with this story and the day she finished it I went home and was RAVING about it and either my brother or mother told me we had a copy of it somewhere that belonged to my brother but he never muched cared for it. I went rummaging and found it and it became mine. :D<br />I still have the same copy of the book! I have read it many times over the years. I love the life Danny and his father live. I think they are a beautiful family. <br /><br />This is a really great kids book...okay a bit morally questionable at times (father is a poacher and they plot to make off with LOADS of pheasants from the local rich guys forest) but its still a really great kids book! </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13239957975877985678">On the face, seems a simple book; Danny and his father live in a caravan with very few luxuries, strangely Danny's father harbours a deep secret. He is a poacher loves a good pheasant. Danny's father comes from a long line of poachers, Danny's grandfather had in fact nearly perfected the art of poaching pheasants. And then Danny tries his Master Plan which involves poaching of 250 birds the entire flock of birds carefully bred and nurtured by Mr Hazell. Yes they do succeed, however with mixed re</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13239957975877985678">On the face, seems a simple book; Danny and his father live in a caravan with very few luxuries, strangely Danny's father harbours a deep secret. He is a poacher loves a good pheasant. Danny's father comes from a long line of poachers, Danny's grandfather had in fact nearly perfected the art of poaching pheasants. And then Danny tries his Master Plan which involves poaching of 250 birds the entire flock of birds carefully bred and nurtured by Mr Hazell. Yes they do succeed, however with mixed results!<br />What Roald Dahl really wants to point out is the snobbishness of the the middle class (now turned classy because of newly acquired wealth)killing pheasants just to invite some Lords for the hunting party and not for the enjoyment of the meat, nor for the enjoyment of sport. I loved the part where Danny and his father realise that everything is best had in small measures, it is never too good to be greedy <br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3392563152946467892">I loved this book as a kid and the re-read as an adult did not disappoint. In fact, started last night and I read it in just two sittings. <br /><br />This is the story of a father and son and their adventure together. Danny's mum died when he was a baby and he was brought up by his dad who is the most wonderful dad in the whole world (according to Danny). Danny and his dad live in a little gypsy caravan behind the petrol filling station which his dad runs. One night Danny wakes to discover his father is mi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3392563152946467892">I loved this book as a kid and the re-read as an adult did not disappoint. In fact, started last night and I read it in just two sittings. <br /><br />This is the story of a father and son and their adventure together. Danny's mum died when he was a baby and he was brought up by his dad who is the most wonderful dad in the whole world (according to Danny). Danny and his dad live in a little gypsy caravan behind the petrol filling station which his dad runs. One night Danny wakes to discover his father is missing from the caravan and this leads him into the discovery of his fathers secret. A secret which it later appears half the village is in on! But it leads to an amazing adventure and one which sees Danny declared as the Champion of the World!<br /><br />This is one of Roald Dahl's less zany books but still a great. Definitely one to read with the nephews in years to come! </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1298942881731532616">This was one of my all-time favorites when I was a kid. I read it several times. And now my son loves it, too!<br /><br />It is a father/son story, but all the more poignant because Dahl's dad died when Dahl was quite young. The book blurb says Dahl learned poaching from a friend.<br /><br />Now that I am an adult I see that it (perhaps unintentionally) poses the question of whether it is okay to steal from someone who is horrible and rich? Danny and his dad are sort of like Robin Hood in this book. Editted to add: I h</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1298942881731532616">This was one of my all-time favorites when I was a kid. I read it several times. And now my son loves it, too!<br /><br />It is a father/son story, but all the more poignant because Dahl's dad died when Dahl was quite young. The book blurb says Dahl learned poaching from a friend.<br /><br />Now that I am an adult I see that it (perhaps unintentionally) poses the question of whether it is okay to steal from someone who is horrible and rich? Danny and his dad are sort of like Robin Hood in this book. Editted to add: I have read some reviews, and a lot of people get hung up about the poaching business. When I was a child, poaching (for me, at least) was so far out of the realm of possibility it might as well have been fantasy. I think it is something important to talk about with your child, but the poaching does not make this a bad book.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer735310375">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1136752434225581337">I've read this ten times or more, so it was no surprise how wonderful it was, but I'd forgotten how vivid some of the language is. A glob of spit sits on dry dust "like an oyster," "little sparks of gold shining through the trees" at twilight - dozens of small flourishes of observation that would grace a literary novel. This is one of my favorite books. I'm so glad it exists.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_904248460">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/904248460?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 18, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/29767877-jared-little" class="user" title="Jared Little">Jared Little</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6690.Danny_the_Champion_of_the_World" title="Hardcover 9780375814259" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/29767877-jared-little?shelf=traditional-literature" class="actionLinkLite">traditional-literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer904248460">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3205216650778933620">This book is required reading for our 6th grade students, and I got my hands on a copy the other day. While I never read this book as a youth, I appreciate it's fantastical english humor and Roald Dahl wit.<br /><br />Danny is the son of a widowed man named William who live in rural England. The two men live in a gypsy caravan and William works at a filling station. Unbeknownst to Danny, William is also a poacher, and often takes local pheasants. When William has a run in with a local baron, Danny and Willi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3205216650778933620">This book is required reading for our 6th grade students, and I got my hands on a copy the other day. While I never read this book as a youth, I appreciate it's fantastical english humor and Roald Dahl wit.<br /><br />Danny is the son of a widowed man named William who live in rural England. The two men live in a gypsy caravan and William works at a filling station. Unbeknownst to Danny, William is also a poacher, and often takes local pheasants. When William has a run in with a local baron, Danny and William decide to teach him a lesson by capturing all of the local pheasants so the baron cannot hunt them. The pheasants end up being given sleeping pills and scratching up the Baron's car. The Baron is shamed and Danny and William bring home many pheasants to eat.<br /><br />This is a fun book to teach, and I have seen many interesting lessons come out of it. It is also a piece of classic literature for students to enjoy. I would teach it as an example of traditional literature and possibly use it to teach the traditional story arch of rising action, climax, and falling action.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3205216650778933620">...more</a>

          </span>

  <a href="/user/show/14018997-jordan-davidson" class="left imgcol" title="Jordan Davidson"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1435210307p2/14018997.jpg" alt="Jordan Davidson" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1273037974?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 23, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/14018997-jordan-davidson" class="user" title="Jordan Davidson">Jordan Davidson</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6690.Danny_the_Champion_of_the_World" title="Hardcover 9780375814259" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/14018997-jordan-davidson?shelf=english-355" class="actionLinkLite">english-355</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1273037974">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11307195366613884359">Danny the Champion of the World<br />Roald Dahl<br />Puffin Books, 2007 (reprint)<br /><br />Summary: Danny learns that his beloved father has a well-kept secret: he’s an illegal peasant poacher, who takes special pleasure in poaching pheasants from Hazell’s Wood. This wood is owned by Mr. Victor Hazell, a filthy rich beer entrepreneur with a foul temper and a mean disposition. One night, Danny’s father is caught in a trap while poaching from the wood. After Danny frees him, the two of them concoct a plan to get reveng</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11307195366613884359">Danny the Champion of the World<br />Roald Dahl<br />Puffin Books, 2007 (reprint)<br /><br />Summary: Danny learns that his beloved father has a well-kept secret: he’s an illegal peasant poacher, who takes special pleasure in poaching pheasants from Hazell’s Wood. This wood is owned by Mr. Victor Hazell, a filthy rich beer entrepreneur with a foul temper and a mean disposition. One night, Danny’s father is caught in a trap while poaching from the wood. After Danny frees him, the two of them concoct a plan to get revenge on Mr. Hazell and become peasant-poaching extraordinaires. <br /><br />Genre: Modern Fantasy.<br /><br />Content Warnings: Criminal activity, character death (prior to the book’s beginning).<br /><br />My Opinion: Roald Dahl was one of my favorite writers when I was a kid, but I never read this book until now. After reading it, I think I have a new favorite work of his. Roald Dahl was always very skillfull at weaving themes and morals into his stories in creative and innovative ways, but his morals sometimes seemed a bit heavy-handed. In this story, they’re much more subtle and, accordingly, much more beautiful in their subtlety. I also loved that this storyline was (slightly) less outlandish than most of his other works. It’s still pretty out-there, but not as much as a story about a giant, or a smart girl with telekinetic powers, or a fantasyland of candy contained within a factory. Highly recommended.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11307195366613884359">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('b+vqiY+/59CjiPqMkPJVN82NnLCMCy52n/iSG26KdrUKP9VafW3zKi9Qjjfuk7OFhHpfqcXWadz18ZeJoh+A8A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Vt/RvEk+mD2VVg0HYZoVG9ewlyL1IzpBBl0smwO5lBUzC+5vu+yMxxmOebwf+/OpnkdUO7z+fetsVCkJzyxiUA==')})
  }

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/4273.Roald_Dahl">About Roald Dahl</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/4273.Roald_Dahl"><img alt="4273" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1311554908p2/4273.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer8974266662679850609">Roald Dahl was a British novelist, short story writer and screenwriter of Norwegian descent, who rose to prominence in the 1940's with works for both children and adults, and became one of the world's bestselling authors.<br /><br />Dahl's first published work, inspired by a meeting with C. S. Forester, was Shot Down Over Libya. Today the story is published as "A Piece of Cake". The story, about his wartime a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8974266662679850609">Roald Dahl was a British novelist, short story writer and screenwriter of Norwegian descent, who rose to prominence in the 1940's with works for both children and adults, and became one of the world's bestselling authors.<br /><br />Dahl's first published work, inspired by a meeting with C. S. Forester, was Shot Down Over Libya. Today the story is published as "A Piece of Cake". The story, about his wartime adventures, was bought by the Saturday Evening Post for $900, and propelled him into a career as a writer. Its title was inspired by a highly inaccurate and sensationalized article about the crash that blinded him, which claimed he had been shot down instead of simply having to land because of low fuel.<br /><br />His first children's book was The Gremlins, about mischievous little creatures that were part of RAF folklore. The book was commissioned by Walt Disney for a film that was never made, and published in 1943. Dahl went on to create some of the best-loved children's stories of the 20th century, such as Charlie and the Chocolate Factory, Matilda and James and the Giant Peach.<br /><br />He also had a successful parallel career as the writer of macabre adult short stories, usually with a dark sense of humour and a surprise ending. Many were originally written for American magazines such as Ladies Home Journal, Harper's, Playboy and The New Yorker, then subsequently collected by Dahl into anthologies, gaining world-wide acclaim. Dahl wrote more than 60 short stories and they have appeared in numerous collections, some only being published in book form after his death. His stories also brought him three Edgar Awards: in 1954, for the collection Someone Like You; in 1959, for the story The Landlady; and in 1980, for the episode of Tales of the Unexpected based on "Skin".</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8974266662679850609">...more</a>

    </div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/824600-danny-the-champion-of-the-world">Quotes from Danny The Champio...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div tyle="padding-bottom:15px" class="stacked">
            <span class="readable">“I was glad my father was an eye-smiler. It meant he never gave me a fake smile because it's impossible to make your eyes twinkle if you aren't feeling twinkly yourself. A mouth-smile is different. You can fake a mouth-smile any time you want, simply by moving your lips. I've also learned that a real mouth-smile always has an eye-smile to go with it. So watch out, I say, when someone smiles at you but his eyes stay the same. It's sure to be a phony.”</span>
            <nobr>
              —
              <a href="/quotes/236390-i-was-glad-my-father-was-an-eye-smiler-it-meant" class="actionLinkLite">265 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div tyle="padding-bottom:15px" class="stacked">
            <span class="readable">“A stodgy parent is no fun at all. What a child wants and deserves is a parent who is SPARKY”</span>
            <nobr>
              —
              <a href="/quotes/706837-a-stodgy-parent-is-no-fun-at-all-what-a" class="actionLinkLite">9 likes</a>
            </nobr>
